<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="course-purpose">COURSE PURPOSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#course-purpose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The purpose of this module is to enable students gain understanding of various leadership and management skills to promote the development of high-quality hospital services and community health care.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="expected-learning-outcomes">Expected Learning Outcomes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#expected-learning-outcomes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Upon successful completion of this module, students should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain the various leadership styles and management functions.</li>
<li>Identify various sources of health care financing</li>
<li>Demonstrate understanding on why people resist change</li>
<li>Identify various sources of health data and information</li>
<li>Describe the procurement process of medical products, vaccines and technology.</li>
<li>Identify different strategies for time management in a healthcare facility.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="module-content">Module content.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#module-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Introduction to Leadership and Management: Concepts, theories, functions and management styles, missions and visions, core values, policies, concepts of change management, relationship between leadership and management; organizational behavior and group dynamics.</p>
<p>b) Communication and networking: public speaking, report writing, networking, advocacy, negation partnership, inter/intra-sectoral collaboration, conducting meetings.</p>
<p>c) Human resource management; concepts and principles, recruitment, orientation, deployment, performance appraisal, job description and job analysis, counselling and coaching, motivation, work climate, conflict resolution and discipline issues; grievances, code of regulations, managing change, continuous professional development, occupational hazards, planning meetings, logistic management.</p>
<p>d) Time management; Time management techniques.</p>
<p>e) Public finance management; sources of finance (government, donors, revolving funds, CDF etc.). Healthcare financing, financial procedures and mechanisms, community. National and international sources for healthcare delivery- proposal writing, resource mobilization and management, budgeting budget types, the role of parliament, treasury the controller and auditor general in public financial management, sources of health care financing, financial accounting systems and mechanisms, accounting documents-imp rest, vouchers, perdiem, facility improvement funds, salaries and wages, allowances, vote books.</p>
<p>f) Commodities and supplies management; principles of supplies cycle, procurement and management of supplies and nurse's role in procurement; selection, procurement, distribution and use, inventory management procedures, procurement procedures, ethical and legal implications in commodity and supply management, commodity management cycle-assessment.</p>
<p>g) Health information system; definition of health information, sources, types, systems of health information, data collection methods, storage and analysis, information utilization; utilization, policy development, decision making.</p>
<p>h) Law governing healthcare practice; definition of law, Kenya new constitution and its application on health services; the different acts in health practice; public health act, food,</p>
<p>Health systems management This document is available on</p>
<p>3</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>drugs and chemical act, nurses act, workman compensation act, children and young persons, succession act, mental health act and criminal penal code.</p>
<p>Entrepreneurship opportunities; educational, scholarships, employment, private practice and other opportunities, preparation for employment to include letter writing, resumes, preparation for interviews.</p>
<p>i) Project management/ planning-principles, concepts, the importance of planning, project planning, proposal writing, types of plans, annual operational plans, annual, departmental and individual plans, project planning process, cycle, situation analysis, feedback, prioritization, developing implementation plans, budgeting, techniques for public involvement.</p>
<p><strong>Community development</strong>: Concepts—community work, group work, case work, community organization; types of community projects—income generating, on-income generating, national projects; Role of the nurse in community development: identification of community needs and community diagnosis; Identification of projects; community development approaches; multidisciplinary approach, directive, non-directive, bureaucratic community participation, community care; Process of project planning: project identification, planning implementation, evaluation.</p>
<p>j) Quality assurance in health services; concepts, principles, quality assurance in healthcare setting, methods and tools of measuring quality, standards in measuring quality; management of quality nursing and health Services—Definition, nursing care modalities (primary nursing, team nursing, case assignment, functional nursing); historical development of quality systems; process-structure outcomes (procedures, policies, standards).</p>
<p>k) Monitoring and evaluation: concepts, types, processes; monitoring and evaluation tools, performance indicators and targets, performance standards, work breakdown schedules, work plans, logical framework approach: <strong>Reports</strong>; types, formats, characteristics of a good report.</p>
<p>l) Disaster management; Introduction, definition of terms, types of disasters and emergencies, phases, disaster management cycle (preparedness, response, mitigation, management of accidents).</p>
<p>Health systems management</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="health-systems-management">HEALTH SYSTEMS MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-systems-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Health systems management or health care systems management describes the leadership and general management of hospitals, hospital networks, and/or health care systems.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251222-9fc101de.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg">
Figure 1. The WHO Health Systems Framework</p>
<p>In international use, the term refers to management at all levels.</p>
<p>Health systems management ensures that;</p>
<p>a. Specific outcomes are attained
b. Departments within a health facility are running smoothly
c. Right people are in the right jobs,
d. People know what is expected of them
e. Resources are used efficiently
f. All departments are working towards a common goal for mutual development and growth.</p>
<p>Health systems management This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-one-introduction-to-leadership-and-management">CHAPTER ONE: INTRODUCTION TO LEADERSHIP AND MANAGEMENT.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-one-introduction-to-leadership-and-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Leadership- Leadership is the ability to influence, inspire and help others become their best selves, building their skills and achieving goals along the way. Leadership is also how you, as an individual, choose to lead your life.</p>
<p>Management. Management is the process of getting activities completed efficiently and effectively with and through other people.</p>
<p>It is also referred to as the art of making things happen with the help of resources.</p>
<p>Management is required for an established life and is essential for managing all types of organisations. Managing life implies getting everything done to accomplish the aspirations of life and maintaining an establishment.</p>
<p>This means getting things done with and by other people to fulfill its objectives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="levels-of-management">Levels Of Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are 3 levels of management in the ranking order of an establishment and these are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Top-level management</li>
<li>Middle-level management</li>
<li>Lower-level management</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="top-level-management">Top Level Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#top-level-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>They comprise of the senior-most executives of the organization. They are normally regarded as the Chairman, the Chief Executive Officer (CEO), and the Chief Operating Officer (COO). Top management is a team consisting of managers from various operational levels.</p>
<p>These top-level managers are accountable for the progress and continuation of the organization. They investigate the trading atmosphere and its connections for the survival of the health facility. They form the overall organisational aims and approaches for their accomplishment. They are held responsible for all the pursuits of the organization and for its influence on the society.</p>
<p>Health systems management</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="middle-level-management">Middle Level Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#middle-level-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is the connection between top and lower-level managers. They are lower to the top managers and above to the first line managers. They are normally called as division heads, for instance. Middle management is accountable for executing and regulating systems generated by the top management.</p>
<p>At the same time, they are liable for all the actions of the first-line managers. Their principal task is to bring out the plans formed by the top managers. For this purpose, they have to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Understand the procedures outlined by the top management</li>
<li>Guarantee that their staff has the required workers</li>
<li>Designate certain tasks and duties to them, and drive them to accomplish the aspired objectives.</li>
<li>Interact with other departments for the stable operation of the company. At the same time, they are subject to all the actions of the first-line managers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lower-level-management">Lower-Level Management.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lower-level-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Managers and supervisors make up the lower level of the management in the hierarchy of the any organization. Supervisors immediately manage the efforts of the workforce. Their power and ability are defined according to the maps drawn by the top management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theories-of-leadership">THEORIES OF LEADERSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-contingency-theory">1. Contingency Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-contingency-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This theory proposes that no one way or style of leadership may be applicable to all situations.</p>
<p>In other words, it recognizes that there might be variables influencing any particular situation, and a leader must choose the right course of action, taking into account those variables.</p>
<p>In this regard, leadership researchers White and Hodgson state, "Effective leadership is about striking the right balance between needs, context, and behavior." The best leaders have not only the right traits but also the ability to assess the needs of their followers, analyze the situation at hand, and act accordingly.</p>
<p>Health systems management

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-situational-leadership-theory">2. Situational Leadership Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-situational-leadership-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Like the Contingency Theory, the Situational Theory stresses the importance of situational variables and doesn't consider anyone's leadership style to be better than the others.</p>
<p>Put forward by US professor, Paul Hersey and leadership guru, Ken Blanchard, the situational theory is a combination of two factors; the leadership style and the maturity levels of the followers. According to this theory, different situations demand different styles of leadership and decision-making. Leaders must act by judging the situation they are facing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-transformational-leadership-theory">3. Transformational Leadership Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-transformational-leadership-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Transformational Leadership theory, also known as Relationship theories, focuses on the relationship between the leaders and followers. This theory talks about the kind of leader who is inspirational and charismatic, encouraging their followers to transform and become better at a task.</p>
<p>Transformational leaders typically motivated by their ability to show their followers the significance of the task and the higher good involved in performing it. These leaders are not only focused on the team's performance but also give individual team members the required push to reach his or her potential. These leadership theories will help you to sharp your Skill.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-transactional-theories">4. Transactional Theories<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-transactional-theories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Transactional Theories, also referred to as Management theories or exchange leadership theories, revolve around the role of supervision, organization, and teamwork. These leadership theories consider rewards and punishments as the basis for leadership actions. This is one of the oft-used theories in business, and the proponents of this leadership style use rewards and punishments to motivate employees.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-behavioral-theory">5. Behavioral Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-behavioral-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the Behavioral Theory, the emphasis shifts from the traits or qualities of leaders to their behaviors and actions. In sharp contrast to the Great Man Theory and the trait approach to leadership, this theory considers effective leadership to be the result of many learned or acquired skills. It proposes that an individual can learn to become a good leader. This is one of the best leadership theories.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Great Man Theory of Leadership</li>
</ol>
<p>This is one of the earliest leadership theories and is based on the assumption that leadership is an inborn phenomenon and that leaders are "born" rather than "made." According to this theory, a person capable of leading has the personality traits of a leader; charm, confidence, intellect, communication skills, and social aptitude; from birth, which set them apart. This theory emphasizes leadership as a quality that you either possess or you don't; it isn't something that you can learn.</p>
<p>While the theory sounds pretty discouraging to those wanting to learn the ropes of leadership, you might take heart in the fact that most modern theorists dismiss it and even by some leaders themselves. It's still an interesting take on leadership and one that highlights the qualities of great leaders, which have more or less remained unchanged over time.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Trait Theory of Leadership</li>
</ol>
<p>This theory walks in the footsteps of the Great Man theory in assuming that leaders are born with traits that make them more suitable for the role of a leader than others who lack those natural-born traits.</p>
<p>As such, the theory pinpoints certain qualities such as intelligence, accountability, sense of responsibility, and creativity, among others, that lets an individual excel at leadership.</p>
<p>Management functions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Planning is the purpose of ascertaining in advance what is supposed to be done and who has to do it. This signifies establishing goals in advance and promoting a way of delivering them effectively and efficiently.</li>
<li>Organising is the administrative operation of specifying grouping tasks, duties, authorising power and designating resources needed to carry out a particular system. Once a definite plan has been set for the completion of an organisational intent, the organising party reviews the actions and resources expected to execute the program. It ascertains what actions and resources are needed. It determines who will do a distinct job, where and when it will be done.</li>
</ul>
<p>Health systems management This document is available on</p>
<p>Studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Staffing is obtaining the best resources for the right job. A significant perspective of management is to make certain that the appropriate people with the apt skills are obtainable in the proper places and times to achieve the goals of the company. This is also called the human resource operations and it includes activities such as selection, placement, recruitment and coaching of employees.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Directing involves, leading and encouraging the employees to complete the tasks allocated to them. This entails building an environment that inspires employees to do their best. Motivation and leadership are two chief elements of direction.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Directing also includes communicating efficiently as well as managing employees at the workplace. Motivating workers means simply building an atmosphere that urges them to want to work. Leadership is inspiring others to do what the manager wants them to do.</p>
<ul>
<li>Controlling is the process of assessing the organization’s progress towards accomplishments of organizational goals and objectives. The job of controlling comprises ascertaining criteria of performance, computing the current performance, comparing this with organised rules and taking remedial action where any divergence is observed. Here management should ascertain what activities and outputs are important to progress, how and where they can be regulated and who should have the power to take remedial response.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leadership-styles">LEADERSHIP STYLES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leadership-styles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Throughout history, great leaders have emerged with particular leadership styles in providing direction, implementing plans and motivating people. These can be broadly grouped into 5 different categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Authoritarian Leadership</li>
<li>Democratic Leadership</li>
<li>Laissez-faire leadership</li>
<li>Transactional Leadership</li>
<li>Transformational Leadership</li>
</ul>
<p>Health systems management</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Despite these definitions, questions still remain.</p>
<ul>
<li>What is the meaning of each leadership style mentioned above?</li>
<li>What is the difference between the different leadership approaches?</li>
<li>What are the advantages and disadvantages of using each of the leadership styles?</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-authoritarian-leadership">1. Authoritarian Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-authoritarian-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Authoritarian leadership styles allow a leader to impose expectations and define outcomes.</p>
<p>A one-person show can turn out to be successful in situations when a leader is the most knowledgeable in the team. Although this is an efficient strategy in time-constrained periods, creativity will be sacrificed since input from the team is limited.</p>
<p>The authoritarian leadership style is also used when team members need clear guidelines.</p>
<p>An authoritarian leader behaves in a commanding and strongly controlling manner.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Time spent on making crucial decisions can be reduced.</li>
<li>Chain of command can be clearly emphasized.</li>
<li>Mistakes in the implementation of plans can be reduced.</li>
<li>Using authoritarian leadership style creates consistent results.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>A very strict leadership style can sometimes lead to employee rebellion.</li>
<li>It kills employee creativity and innovation.</li>
<li>It reduces group synergy &amp; collaboration.</li>
<li>Group input is reduced dramatically.</li>
<li>Authoritarian leadership increases employee turnover rate.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-democratic-leadership">2. Democratic Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-democratic-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health systems management This document is available on</p>
<p>11</p>
<p>Studio</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In this leadership style, subordinates are involved in making decisions. Unlike the autocratic style, this leadership is centered on subordinates’ contributions. The democratic leader holds final responsibility, but he or she is known to delegate authority to other people, who determine work projects.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The most unique feature of this leadership is that communication is active upward and downward. With respect to statistics, democratic leadership is one of the most preferred styles of leadership, and it entails the following: fairness, competence, creativity, courage, intelligence and honesty.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It increases employee motivation and job satisfaction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It encourages use of employee creativity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A participative leadership style helps in the creation of a strong team.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>High level of productivity can be achieved.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Decision-making processes become time-consuming.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Leaders have a high probability of being apologetic to employees.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication failures can sometimes happen.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Security issues can arise because of transparency in information sharing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor decisions can be made if the employees are unskilled.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-laissez-faire-leadership">3. Laissez-faire leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-laissez-faire-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is also known as, a delegative leadership style, it focuses on delegating initiative to team members. This can be a successful strategy if team members are competent, take responsibility and prefer engaging in individual work. However, disagreements among the members may split and divide a group, leading to poor motivation and low morale.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health systems management</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Experienced employees can take advantage of their competence and experience.</li>
<li>Innovation &amp; creativity is highly valued.</li>
<li>Delegative leadership creates a positive work environment.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Disadvantages:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Command responsibility is not properly defined.</li>
<li>Delegative leadership creates difficulty in adapting to change.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-transactional-leadership">4. Transactional leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-transactional-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Transactional leadership styles use "transactions" between a leader and his or her followers - rewards, punishments and other exchanges - to get the job done. The leader sets clear goals, and team members know how they'll be rewarded for their compliance. This "give and take" leadership style is more concerned with following established routines and procedures in an efficient manner, than with making any transformational changes to an organization.</p>
<p><strong>Advantages:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Leaders create specific, measurable and time-bound goals that are achievable for employees.</li>
<li>Employee motivation and productivity is increased.</li>
<li>Transactional leadership eliminates or minimizes confusion in the chain of command.</li>
<li>It creates a system that is easy to implement for leaders and easy to follow by employees.</li>
<li>Employees can choose reward systems.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Disadvantages:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Innovation &amp; creativity is minimized.</li>
<li>Empathy is not valued.</li>
<li>Transactional leadership creates more followers than leaders among employees.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-transformational-leadership">5. Transformational Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-transformational-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health systems management This document is available on</p>
<p>Studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>In transformational leadership styles, the leader inspires his or her followers with a vision and then encourages and empowers them to achieve it. The leader also serves as a role model for the vision.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages">Advantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It leads to a lower employee turnover rate.</li>
<li>Transformational leadership places high value on corporate vision.</li>
<li>High morale of employees is often experienced.</li>
<li>It uses motivation and inspiration to gain the support of employees.</li>
<li>It is not a coercive approach to leadership.</li>
<li>It places high value on relationships.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages">Disadvantages:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Leaders can deceive employees.</li>
<li>Consistent motivation and constant feedback may be required.</li>
<li>Tasks can't be pushed through without the agreement of employees.</li>
<li>Transformational leadership can sometimes lead to the deviation of protocols and regulations.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-major-difference-between-leadership-and-management-are">The major difference between leadership and management are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-major-difference-between-leadership-and-management-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Leadership, is a virtue of leading people through encouraging them. Management is a process of managing the activities of the organization.
b. Leadership requires trust of followers on his leader. Unlike Management, which needs control of manager over its subordinates.
c. Leadership's askill of influencing others while Management is the quality of the ruling.
d. Leadership demands foresightedness of leader, but Management has a short-range vision.</p>
<p>Health systems management</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>e. In leadership, principles and guidelines are established, whereas, in the case of management, policies and procedures are implemented.
f. Leadership is Proactive. Conversely, management is reactive in nature.
g. Leadership brings change. On the other hand, Management brings stability.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-theories">MANAGEMENT THEORIES.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-theories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="theory-x-and-theory-y">Theory X and theory Y.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theory-x-and-theory-y" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Theory X and theory Y are theories of human motivation. They describe two very different attitudes towards workforce motivation. McGregor thought that the key to connecting self-actualization with work is determined by the managerial trust of subordinates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="theory-x">Theory X.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theory-x" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this theory which has been proved counter-effective in most modern practice, management assumes employees are inherently lazy and will avoid work if they can and they inherently dislike work. As a result of this, management beliefs that workers need to be closely supervised and comprehensive systems of controls developed.</p>
<p><strong>Hierarchy</strong> – A hierarchical structure is needed with narrow span of control at each and every level. According to this theory, employees will show little ambition without incentive and will avoid responsibility.</p>
<p>If the organizational goals are to be met, theory X managers rely heavily on threats and coercion to gain their employees compliance (according to Michael J. Papa). Beliefs of this theory lead to mistrust, highly restrictive supervision, punitive atmosphere etc. Theory X manager tends to believe that everything must end in blaming someone (suspicious always). They will blame the person first without questioning whether it may be the system, policy, or lack of training that deserves the blame. Theory X manager believes that his or her employees do not really want to work but they are out for themselves and that their interest in the job is only money.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theory-y">Theory Y.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theory-y" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In this theory, management assumes employees may be ambitious and self-motivated and exercise self-control. It is believed that employees enjoy their mental and physical work duties and to them, work is as natural as play. They possess the ability for creative problem solving, but their talents are underused in most organizations.</p>
<p><strong>Self-control</strong>- Given the proper conditions, theory Y managers believe that employees will learn to seek out and accept responsibility and to exercise self-control and self-direction in accomplishing objectives to which they are committed. Theory Y managers believe that given the right condition, most people will want to do well at work. They believe that the satisfaction of doing a good job is a strong motivation. Many people interpret theory Y as a positive set of beliefs about workers.</p>
<p>McGregor thinks that theory Y managers are more likely than theory X managers to develop the climate of trust with employees that is required for human resource development, which is a crucial aspect of any organization. This would include managers communicating openly with subordinates, minimizing difference between superior subordinate relationships, creating a comfortable environment, subordinates develop and use their abilities, sharing of decision making and employer is under less pressure than in theory X.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organizational-beahaviour">ORGANIZATIONAL BEAHAVIOUR.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizational-beahaviour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Organizational Behavior (OB) is the study and application of knowledge about how people, individuals, and groups act in organizations. It does this by taking a system approach, meaning it interprets people-organization relationships in terms of the whole person, whole group, whole organization, and whole social system. Its purpose is to build better relationships by achieving human objectives, organizational objectives, and social objectives.</p>
<p>Elements of organizational behaviour.</p>
<ol>
<li>The organization's base rests on management's philosophy, values, vision and goals.</li>
<li>Organizational behaviour drives its culture which is composed of the formal organization, informal organization and the social environment.</li>
<li>The Organizational Behaviour culture determines the type of leadership, communication and group dynamics within the organization.</li>
<li>The workers perceive this as the quality of work life which directs their degree of motivation.</li>
<li>The final outcome is performance, individual satisfaction, and personal growth and development.</li>
<li>To build the model or framework that the organization operates from.</li>
</ol>
<p>Models of organizational behaviour.</p>
<p>There are four major models or frameworks that organizations operate out of.</p>
<p>Model 1: Autocratic.</p>
<p>Basis - The basis of this model is power with a managerial orientation of authority. The employees in turn are oriented towards obedience and dependence on the boss.</p>
<p>Employee needs - The employee need, that is met is subsistence.</p>
<p>Performance Result - The performance result is minimal.</p>
<p>Model 2: Custodial.</p>
<p>Basis - The basis of this model is economic resources with a managerial orientation of money. The employees in turn are oriented towards security and benefits and dependence on the organization.</p>
<p>Employee needs - The employee need, that is met is security.</p>
<p>Health systems management
